          "isPartOf_label", "areaCode", "populationTotal", "elevation",
          "maximumElevation", "minimumElevation", "populationDensity",

    reader = csv.DictReader(fin)
    input_cities_list = list(reader)
In [4]:
datatype_dict = {k:[] for k in FIELDS}
In [6]:
''''
The below piece of code is used to generate a dictionary that gives in the data types contained in each of the dictionary fields
'''
for key in datatype_dict:
    for item in input_cities_list[3:]:
        if (item[key] == 'NULL') or (item[key] == ""):
            datatype_dict[key].append(type(None))
            
        elif item[key].startswith('{'):
            datatype_dict[key].append(type(list()))
            
        else:
            try:
                if int(item[key]):
                    datatype_dict[key].append(type(int()))
            except ValueError:
                try: 
                    if float(item[key]):
                        datatype_dict[key].append(type(float()))
                except ValueError:    
                    datatype_dict[key].append(type(str()))
In [7]:
for key in datatype_dict:
    datatype_dict[key] = set(datatype_dict[key])

In [9]:
#This function fixes the values in the area key of the data file to take a float value. If the value field is a list, I take the 
#value with the most signifiant digits.
def fix_area(area):
    if (area == 'Null') or (area == "") or (area == 'NULL'):
        return None
    
    elif area.startswith('{'):
        area = area.strip('{}')
        area = area.split('|')
        #print area
        reobj = re.compile(r'(\d*?)(0*)(\.0?)')
        matched_string_0 = reobj.match(str(float(area[0]))).group(1)
        matched_string_1 = reobj.match(str(float(area[1]))).group(1)
        #print matched_string_0
        #print matched_string_1
        
        if len(matched_string_0) > len(matched_string_1):
            #print 'gudia'
            return float(area[0])
        elif len(matched_string_0) < len(matched_string_1):
            #print 'hey'
            return float(area[1])
        else:
            if matched_string_0 > matched_string_1:
                #print 'hello'
                return float(area[0])
            else:
                #print 'parry'
                return float(area[1])

    else:
        try:
            if float(area):
                return float(area)
        except ValueError:
            return None

for item in input_cities_list[3:]:

In [11]:
#Similar to the fix_area function, this function returns a list of names for each entry instead of inconsistent data types
def fix_name(name):
    name_list = []
    if (name == 'NULL') or (name == 'Null') or (name == ""):
        return name_list
    elif name.startswith('{'):
        name = name.strip('{}')
        name_list = name.split('|')
        return name_list
    else:
        name_list.append(name)
        return name_list
In [12]:

    #print item['areaLand']
    #if item['areaLand'] != 'NULL':
        #print item['areaLand']
    item['name'] = fix_name(item['name'])

#This function doesn't do anything but just checks whether whether the location is represented by float values
def check_loc(point, lat, longi):
    point = point.strip()
    point = point.split()
    if (lat.strip() == point[0]):
        if (longi.strip() == point[1]):
            return True
        else:
            return False
    else:
        return False
